     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        Mushishi
       </b>
      </i>
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
        Japanese
       </a>
       :
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">
       manga
      </a>
      series written and illustrated by
      <a href="/wiki/Yuki_Urushibara" title="Yuki Urushibara">
       Yuki Urushibara
      </a>
      . It was
      <a href="/wiki/Serial_(literature)" title="Serial (literature)">
       serialized
      </a>
      in
      <i>
       Afternoon Seasons Zkan
      </i>
      from 1999 to 2002, and in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monthly_Afternoon" title="Monthly Afternoon">
        Monthly Afternoon
       </a>
      </i>
      from December 2002 to August 2008. The individual chapters were collected and released into ten
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankbon">
        tankbon
       </a>
      </i>
      volumes by
      <a href="/wiki/Kodansha" title="Kodansha">
       Kodansha
      </a>
      . Those volumes were localized to North America by
      <a href="/wiki/Del_Rey_Manga" title="Del Rey Manga">
       Del Rey
      </a>
      between January 2007 and August 2010. The series follows Ginko, a man who dedicates himself to keeping people protected from supernatural creatures called Mushi.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      has been adapted into an
      <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">
       anime
      </a>
      television series by
      <a href="/wiki/Artland_(company)" title="Artland (company)">
       Artland
      </a>
      which aired in
      <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" title="Fuji Television">
       Fuji Television
      </a>
      between October 2005 and June 2006. It has been licensed by
      <a href="/wiki/Funimation" title="Funimation">
       Funimation
      </a>
      to its release in North America, while
      <a href="/wiki/Madman_Entertainment" title="Madman Entertainment">
       Madman Entertainment
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Revelation_Films" title="Revelation Films">
       Revelation Films
      </a>
      licensed it for Australia and the United Kingdom respectively. A second anime series aired between April and December 2014, which has been licensed in North America by
      <a href="/wiki/Aniplex_of_America" title="Aniplex of America">
       Aniplex of America
      </a>
      , with two television specials airing in 2014. A live-action film, directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Katsuhiro_Otomo" title="Katsuhiro Otomo">
       Katsuhiro Otomo
      </a>
      , was released in late 2006, and a second one has been announced for a 2015 release. It has also spawned a video game and many types of
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      -related merchandise.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      manga has been well received both by the public and critics. In Japan, it has frequently ranked in the weekly Top Ten list of best-selling manga, and the entire series has sold over 3.8 million copies. Both the manga and the anime have received several awards such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_Manga_Award" title="Kodansha Manga Award">
       Kodansha Manga Award
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Anime_Award" title="Tokyo Anime Award">
       Tokyo Anime Award
      </a>
      , and numerous publications have praised them.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">
       Plot
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The story features ubiquitous creatures called Mushi
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      that often display what appear as
      <a href="/wiki/Supernatural" title="Supernatural">
       supernatural
      </a>
      powers. It is implied that there are many more lifeforms more primitive than "normal" living things such as animals, plants, fungi and bacteria, and Mushi is the most primitive of all. Due to their ethereal nature most humans are incapable of perceiving Mushi and are oblivious to their existence, but there are a few who possess the ability to see and interact with Mushi. One such person is Ginko
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      , the main character of the series. He employs himself as a Mushi Master
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">
        ,
       </span>
       <i>
        mushi-shi
       </i>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      , traveling from place to place to research Mushi and aid people suffering from problems caused by them. The series is an episodic anthology in which the only common elements among episodes are Ginko and the various types of Mushi. There is no overarching plotline.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Characters_and_setting">
       Characters and setting
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Characters and setting">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Urushibara stated that
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      is set in an imaginary time between the
      <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">
       Edo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Meiji_period" title="Meiji period">
       Meiji periods
      </a>
      , featuring some 19th-century technology but with Japan still as a
      <a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">
       "closed country"
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Due to the episodic nature of the series, there are very few recurring characters. The most frequently seen character is an otherworldly-looking man named Ginko, who is voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Yuto_Nakano" title="Yuto Nakano">
       Yuto Nakano
      </a>
      in the original version and by
      <a href="/wiki/Travis_Willingham" title="Travis Willingham">
       Travis Willingham
      </a>
      in the English dub.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staff_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-staff-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ginko is a rare person who attracts mushi, which inspires a lifestyle of constant wandering. He also smokes in order to keep the mushi away. In terms of personality, Ginko is generally laid back and focused on his work. However, he can be very serious when it comes to protecting people from mushi. He also often stresses that the mushi are not evil, but merely trying to survive like everyone else. A majority of the stories do not focus on Ginko, but rely on him as a catalyst to move the story forward by diagnosing or curing mushi-related illnesses and phenomena.
     </p>
     <p>
      Other recurring appearances are limited to a collector named Adashino
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      , who appears in episodes 5, 10, and briefly in 18 of season 1, as well as in the first special, and episode 8 of season 2; Tany
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      and her caretaker Tama
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      , who appear in episode 20 of season 1, and in both special chapters; and Isaza, from the nomad group in episode 26 of the first season, who later shows up in episode 1 of the second season (with a brief cameo in the first special). Nui
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      , a Mushi master who appears only in episode 12, can be heard narrating some of the opening and closing lines characteristic of each episode. Respectively,
      <a href="/wiki/Y%C5%ABji_Ueda" title="Yji Ueda">
       Yji Ueda
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mika_Doi" title="Mika Doi">
       Mika Doi
      </a>
      voice Adashino and Nui in the original version, while
      <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Huber" title="Chuck Huber">
       Chuck Huber
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Seman" title="Jennifer Seman">
       Jennifer Seman
      </a>
      provide their voices in the English dub.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
       Media
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Media">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Manga">
       Manga
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Manga">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Written and illustrated by Yuki Urushibara, it debuted as an
      <a href="/wiki/One-shot_(comics)" title="One-shot (comics)">
       one-shot
      </a>
      in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Monthly_Afternoon" title="Monthly Afternoon">
        Monthly Afternoon
       </a>
      </i>
      on January 25, 1999.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Later, it was
      <a href="/wiki/Serial_(literature)" title="Serial (literature)">
       serialized
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Kodansha" title="Kodansha">
       Kodansha
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Seinen_manga" title="Seinen manga">
        seinen
       </a>
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_manga_magazines" title="List of manga magazines">
       manga magazine
      </a>
      <i>
       Afternoon Seasons Zkan
      </i>
      from 1999 to 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It moved to
      <i>
       Monthly Afternoon
      </i>
      on December 25, 2002 and was serialized until August 25, 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kodansha collected the chapters into ten
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tank%C5%8Dbon" title="Tankbon">
        tankbon
       </a>
      </i>
      , and published them under the
      <i>
       Afternoon KC
      </i>
      line from November 22, 2001, to November 21, 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On November 21, 2013, Kodansha started to re-release it under the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aiz%C5%8Dban" title="Aizban">
        aizban
       </a>
      </i>
      format in their
      <i>
       KC Deluxe
      </i>
      line, concluding with the tenth on July 23, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the 2006
      <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">
       Comic-Con
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Del_Rey_Manga" title="Del Rey Manga">
       Del Rey Manga
      </a>
      announced that it had licensed
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      for an English-language translation in North America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Del Rey published the first volume on January 30, 2007, and the last volume, a combined edition covering volumes 8 to 10, was released on July 27, 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2014,
      <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_Comics_USA" title="Kodansha Comics USA">
       Kodansha Comics USA
      </a>
      announced it will publish the manga in digital format late in the year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The manga was also licensed in some countries such in South Korea by
      <a href="/wiki/Daewon_C.I." title="Daewon C.I.">
       Daewon C.I.
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in Italy by
      <a href="/wiki/Star_Comics_(Italy)" title="Star Comics (Italy)">
       Star Comics
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in Spain by
      <a href="/wiki/Norma_Editorial" title="Norma Editorial">
       Norma Editorial
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in France by
      <a href="/wiki/Kana_(publisher)" title="Kana (publisher)">
       Kana
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In addition, two additional chapters were published in the magazine on November 25, 2012 and December 25, 2013, respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hihamukage_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hihamukage-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They were encapsulated into a single
      <i>
       tankbon
      </i>
      titled
      <i>
       Mushishi Tokubetsu-hen: Hihamukage
      </i>
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
          
       </span>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      and released on April 23, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">
       Anime
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Anime">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mushishi_episodes" title="List of Mushishi episodes">
       List of Mushishi episodes
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      anime adaptation was animated by
      <a href="/wiki/Artland_(company)" title="Artland (company)">
       Artland
      </a>
      , directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Hiroshi_Nagahama" title="Hiroshi Nagahama">
       Hiroshi Nagahama
      </a>
      , and produced by a group called "
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      Production Committee",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staff_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-staff-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which consists of
      <a href="/wiki/Marvelous_Entertainment" title="Marvelous Entertainment">
       Marvelous Entertainment
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avex" title="Avex">
       Avex Entertainment
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/SKY_Perfect_Well_Think" title="SKY Perfect Well Think">
       SKY Perfect Well Think
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ep1_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ep1-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first 20 episodes of the series originally aired between October 23, 2005 and March 12, 2006 on
      <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" title="Fuji Television">
       Fuji Television
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstdate_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-firstdate-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        note 1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A digest was broadcast on May 7, 2006 by

      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-venice_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-venice-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-film_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-film-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A second film, that will be based on the manga's last arc, "Suzu no Shizuku," was announced in December 2014 to be released in Summer 2015 in Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-film2_58-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-film2-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From March 18 to 29, 2015, a "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staged_reading" title="Staged reading">
       stage reading
      </a>
      " event, which adapted six chapters from the manga into six separate performances, was held in Tokyo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-stage-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was directed by
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      anime director Hiroshi Nagahama and its original script was written by Kazuaki Nakamura, while the anime voice actors acted as their respective characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_78-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-stage-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The production used
      <a href="/wiki/Augmented_reality" title="Augmented reality">
       augmented reality
      </a>
      on its visuals, which was designed to span a 270 degree field of view.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_78-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-stage-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
       Reception
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mushishi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reception">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The series has won numerous awards; in 2003, the manga was awarded an Excellence Prize for manga at the 7th
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Media_Arts_Festival" title="Japan Media Arts Festival">
       Japan Media Arts Festival
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while in 2006, the series won the
      <a href="/wiki/Kodansha_Manga_Award" title="Kodansha Manga Award">
       Kodansha Manga Award
      </a>
      for general manga.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At the 10th Japan Media Arts Festival, both the anime and manga series were placed among the top 10 in their respective categories for best manga and anime.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The anime series won grand prizes in the categories of television series and best art direction (for Takashi Waki) at the 5th
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Anime_Award" title="Tokyo Anime Award">
       Tokyo Anime Award
      </a>
      competition held at the
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Anime_Fair" title="Tokyo International Anime Fair">
       Tokyo International Anime Fair
      </a>
      in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also ranked 13th in a "Top 20" poll conducted by Japanese anime magazine
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Animage" title="Animage">
        Animage
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the following year,
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      was placed in 9th on Japan's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agency_for_Cultural_Affairs" title="Agency for Cultural Affairs">
       Agency for Cultural Affairs
      </a>
      's list of best manga, as well as ranked in 6th place on its list of best anime.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Adult_Library_Services_Association" title="Young Adult Library Services Association">
       Young Adult Library Services Association
      </a>
      also listed the manga among 33 titles with "good quality literature and appealing reading for teens" in 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      was also well received by Japanese-language readers. The ten volumes have sold over 3.8 million copies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-film_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-film-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Individual volumes frequently appeared on the weekly lists of best-selling manga there.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Further, the eighth volume was the ninth best-selling manga of
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">
       Amazon.com
      </a>
      in the first half of 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A similar feat was achieved by the last volume which was ranked 49th in the
      <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">
       Oricon
      </a>
      list of best-selling manga of the first half of 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In North America, ICv2 has listed the manga among the "Top 300 Graphic Novels" of the month twice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Readers of
      <a href="/wiki/About.com" title="About.com">
       About.com
      </a>
      voted it the best
      <i>
       seinen
      </i>
      manga released in North America in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      was chosen as the best manga of 2007 by Deb Aoki of About.com,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aoki_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-aoki-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while it was elected the best anime series of 2007 by
      <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">
       Anime News Network
      </a>
      's Carl Kimlinger,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kim_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-kim-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was ranked seventh on
      <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">
       IGN
      </a>
      's Ramsey Isler top anime of 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isler_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-isler-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Aoki called it "a rare breed of manga: a smartly-written, original story that's told with simple yet mesmerizing imagery."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aoki_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-aoki-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Similarly, Kimlinger declared that "Its hypnotic rhythm, humanism, and naturalist's eye for beauty give it a charm that far outstrips mere entertainment value."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kim_95-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-kim-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jason_Thompson_(writer)" title="Jason Thompson (writer)">
       Jason Thompson
      </a>
      's said it may be "too mellow" for some readers, although he praised it for having a "very original vision, with a sort of 'flowing life' of its own, a biologist's precision mixed with creepy fairytales and a surreal, dreamy feel."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its storytelling was highly praised; Isler deemed it as "near flawless",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isler_96-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-isler-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while Pop Culture Shock's Ken Haley labeled it "an enjoyable and intriguing read",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and it was praised for its "short, spooky and breathtaking stories" by Shirl Sazynski of Sequential Tart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Writing for Manga Life, Joy Kim stated that despite not having a central story, which allows to start reading
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      at any volume, "the quality of the storytelling" will make fans want to read it completely.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The "quiet and subtle stories that evoke strong emotions with great story crafting and a fine tune to the essence of what moves people" is the main appeal of the series, according to Holly Ellingwood of Active Anime.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both Ed Sizemore and Avi Weinryb, writing for Comics Worth Reading and Comic Book Bin respectively, said
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      has something to tell to readers, with the former commenting "If you want a manga to make you stop and think, this is the manga for you."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Mushi-Shi -Next Passage-
      </i>
      has been well received by fans; almost all DVD and Blu-Ray volumes made the top-20 list of the respective media on
      <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">
       Oricon
      </a>
      best-selling charts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        note 4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Critically-wise, Hope Chapman of
      <a href="/wiki/Anime_News_Network" title="Anime News Network">
       Anime News Network
      </a>
      praised the maintenance of the visual quality and the improvement on the stories, declaring "
      <i>
       Mushi-Shi
      </i>
      is quickly evolving from an excellent series of fables about the natural world to a wholly unique masterpiece that a written review can't really do justice by."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Chapman dubbed it "one of the all-time greatest animated anthology series".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Fandom Post's Kory Cerjak stated the series "is perhaps one of the most innovative shows out there in terms of storytelling."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ben Huber of Japanator said it has a "soothing music and beautiful art", and affirmed "most anime struggle to create relatable and compelling characters in 12 or 24 episodes.
      <i>
       Mushishi
      </i>
      does it every week in one goddamn episode... and it does it with grace."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Richard Eisenbeis of
      <a href="/wiki/Kotaku" title="Kotaku">
       Kotaku
      </a>
      said it was worth watching just for its imagery but wrote that "It is a series that is equal parts beautiful and hauntingoften bringing more emotion in a 22-minute episode than most series can bring in their entire runs."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>

       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>

         the third volume placed 18th (DVD) and 11th (Blu-Ray);
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">

           105
